<h2>What is OCaml?</h2>
<p>OCaml is a general-purpose, statically-typed programming language with an emphasis on expressiveness and safety. It was designed in 1996 by Xavier Leroy and his team at INRIA in France as an extension of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ML_(programming_language)" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Meta Language</a> Caml dialect. Although Caml had a powerful type system and functional programming capabilities, it was only ever used in academia. However, by incorporating features such as object-oriented programming while retaining the correctness and conciseness of its predecessor, OCaml became a suitable language for building practical, real-world applications (which is what the O in OCaml formerly stood for Objective, if you were wondering).</p>
<p>OCaml&#8217;s strong type system, inherited from its predecessors, helps ensure code is safe and correct by catching errors at compile-time, while maintaining the flexibility of untyped languages by performing type inference. Not only that, OCaml’s algebraic data types allows for powerful pattern-matching capabilities, making it easy to match, extract and manipulate data in a concise and expressive way.</p>
<p>Many of OCaml’s features encourage programming in the functional style, such as preferring recursion and higher-order functions over traditional loops and preferring immutable data structures over mutable ones. However, it acknowledges that certain tasks  such as working with files and writing in-place algorithms can be difficult to accomplish using only functional methods. As a result, OCaml offers support for multiple programming paradigms like imperative and object-oriented programming, giving developers flexibility to choose the best paradigm for their problem.</p>
<p>OCaml is also known for performance and ability to easily integrate with other languages, such as C and JavaScript, making it a great choice for building multi-language systems.</p>
<p>As for its applications, OCaml is widely used in academia and research institutions, with many universities like Cornell and Princeton including it in their curriculum to teach functional programming. And although OCaml is relatively niche compared to other languages, it has been used in <a href="https://ocaml.org/industrial-users" target="_blank" rel="noopener">several large-scale industry projects</a> by companies such as Facebook for compilers and static analysis, Jane Street for guaranteeing the correctness of their internal trading systems, Coq for checking mathematical theorems, and Bloomberg for advanced financial derivatives risk management application.<br />
<a href="https://www.classcentral.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone wp-image-79247 size-full" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-1.png" alt="Find your next course." width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-1.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-1-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-1-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<h2>Best Courses Guides Methodology</h2>
<p>I built this ranking following the now tried-and-tested methodology used in previous Best Courses Guides (<a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/category/best-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">you can find them all here</a>). It involves a three-step process:</p>
<ol>
<li aria-level="1"><b>Research:</b> I started by leveraging Class Central’s database with <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subjects" target="_blank" rel="noopener">100K online courses</a> and 200K+ reviews. Then, I made a preliminary selection of <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subject/ocaml" target="_blank" rel="noopener">OCaml courses</a> by rating, reviews, and bookmarks.</li>
<li aria-level="1"><b>Evaluate:</b> I read through reviews on Class Central, Reddit, and course providers to understand what other learners thought about each course and combined it with my own experience as a <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/@Elham" target="_blank" rel="noopener">learner</a>.</li>
<li aria-level="1"><b>Select:</b> Well-made courses were picked if they presented valuable and engaging content and they have to fit in a set of criteria and be ranked accordingly: comprehensive curriculum, affordability, release date, ratings and enrollments.</li>
</ol>
<h2>Course Ranking Statistics</h2>
<p>Here are some aggregate stats about the ranking:</p>
<ul>
<li aria-level="1">All of the courses in this ranking are <b>free</b> or <b>free-to-audit</b>.</li>
<li aria-level="1">All of the courses are suitable for beginners to OCaml. Unfortunately, none of the courses are geared towards complete beginners to programming.</li>
<li aria-level="1">Two of the courses are from universities while the rest are from independent providers.</li>
</ul>
<p>Without further ado, let’s go through the top picks.</p>
<h2 id="anchor-1">1. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/independent-ocaml-programming-correct-efficient-beautiful-121110" target="_blank" rel="noopener">OCaml Programming: Correct + Efficient + Beautiful  (Cornell University)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85426" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/1.-OCaml-Programming_-Correct-Efficient-Beautiful-Cornell-University.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/1.-OCaml-Programming_-Correct-Efficient-Beautiful-Cornell-University.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/1.-OCaml-Programming_-Correct-Efficient-Beautiful-Cornell-University-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/1.-OCaml-Programming_-Correct-Efficient-Beautiful-Cornell-University-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>

<p>The course covers a wide range of topics related to OCaml, including functional programming, correctness and efficiency, data structures, and best software engineering practices.</p>
<p>Prior knowledge programming in some mainstream imperative language (<a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/best-java-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Java</a> and <a href="https://www.freecodecamp.org/news/best-python-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Python</a> preferred) and first-semester standard discrete mathematics is assumed prior to taking this course.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>You’ll start straight away by diving into the basics of OCaml, starting with basic syntax like writing expressions and functions. You’ll quickly familiarize yourself with the functional style of programming through extensive use of OCaml’s REPL.</p>
<p>As you become more comfortable with the language’s distinctive syntax, you’ll find yourself appreciating its underlying principles that help developers write concise yet expressive, correct yet efficient code. For example, OCaml is awesome for <a href="http://ocamlverse.net/content/compilers.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">writing compilers</a> thanks to functional programming concepts such as parametric polymorphism, algebraic data types, higher-order programming, pattern matching. Hence, you’ll study all of these in-depth, along software engineering best practices such as error handling, testing, and documentation.</p>
<p>Not only that, data structures will also be covered in the course, from the ones available in the standard library to more complicated data structures that you’ll implement on your own using both imperative and functional programming. You’ll be able to analyze the efficiency of data structures using amortized analysis and choose the one that suits your use case.</p>
<p>Remember that I mentioned OCaml is great for writing compilers? Well, the final part of this course demystifies compilers enough for you to design and implement some small, special-purpose domain-specific languages (DSLs).</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course consists of 9 chapters. You’ll learn by reading through the chapters and watching the videos. At the end of each chapter except the first, you’ll find exercises for you to practice what you’ve learned. Additionally, the course has a feature called collaborative annotations that allows you to highlight and make private notes that you can share with others.</p>

Due to overwhelming positive feedback, Michael made the videos publicly available for anyone who wants to learn about OCaml, functional programming, and becoming a better programmer.</li>

<h2 id="anchor-2">2. <a href="https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLGC2in6hSHQcmT_cz4t7ePeQtTCkNkvll" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Introduction to Functional Programming in OCaml (Université Paris Diderot)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85432" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-Introduction-to-Functional-Programming-in-OCaml-Universite-Paris-Diderot.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-Introduction-to-Functional-Programming-in-OCaml-Universite-Paris-Diderot.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-Introduction-to-Functional-Programming-in-OCaml-Universite-Paris-Diderot-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-Introduction-to-Functional-Programming-in-OCaml-Universite-Paris-Diderot-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>My second pick for the best OCaml course is <a href="https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLGC2in6hSHQcmT_cz4t7ePeQtTCkNkvll" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Introduction to Functional Programming in OCaml</a> offered by Université de Paris.</p>
<p>This MOOC focuses on teaching the principles of functional programming using the OCaml programming language by emphasizing the use of functions as first-class values to create and manage complex data structures. The course will begin by showing the use of OCaml as a functional programming language alone, and by the end, it’ll demonstrate how OCaml can be utilized as a multi-paradigm language, combining functional and imperative programming styles to get the best of both worlds.</p>
<p>To follow this course, you should already have some basic knowledge of writing simple computer programs in a programming language.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>You’ll begin the course with an overview of the language, starting with its robust type system. OCaml is statically-typed language, but thanks to its flexible type inference you’ll find yourself working with the type-checker rather than against it, and even create your own types. Combined with immutable data structures, such as tuples, records, and trees, you’ll see how they can be used effectively in your programs.</p>
<p>As a functional-first programming language, OCaml emphasizes the concepts of functional programming (FP), including the use of recursion over loops and the treatment of functions as first-class citizens. You’ll gain hands-on experience with key FP concepts such as partial function application, map and fold operations, and more.</p>
<p>By now, you’ve probably gotten a good understanding of how functional programming differs from imperative programming. Imperative programming is useful in some cases though, so you’ll explore OCaml’s imperative constructs such as modules, input/output, and exceptions.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course is 6 weeks long, with the total video watch time adding up to 7 hours. You’ll learn by watching the lecture videos and following along with the examples provided by the instructors.</p>

<h3>Fun Facts</h3>
<ul>
<li aria-level="1">Roberto Di Cosmo is professor of computer science at University Paris Diderot, director of Irill, currently on leave at INRIA. His research interests include functional and parallel programming, type systems, logic, rewriting, and the static analysis of large software collections.</li>
<li aria-level="1">Yann Régis-Gianas teaches computer science at Université Paris-Diderot. His research at the PPS laboratory focuses on the theory and the design of programming languages. He did his PhD in the INRIA team that develops OCaml and is now in the development team of the Coq proof assistant.</li>
<li aria-level="1">Ralf Treinen is professor of computer science at University Paris Diderot. Symbolic constraint solving, verification and application of formal methods to the quality assurance of software components are among his current research interests. He is also a member of Irill.</li>
</ul>

<h2 id="anchor-3">3. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/youtube-programming-with-ocaml-122060" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Programming with OCaml (Anthony Narlock)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85431" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/3.-Programming-with-OCaml-Anthony-Narlock.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/3.-Programming-with-OCaml-Anthony-Narlock.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/3.-Programming-with-OCaml-Anthony-Narlock-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/3.-Programming-with-OCaml-Anthony-Narlock-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/youtube-programming-with-ocaml-122060" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Programming with OCaml</a> teaches the basics of programming in OCaml, especially how it differs from other traditional programming languages.</p>
<p>No prior knowledge of OCaml is required to take this course.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>You’ll start this course by getting familiar with the command line tool `utop`. You&#8217;ll explore OCaml&#8217;s powerful static type system, including its basic types such as integers, floats, booleans, strings, and characters. Additionally, you&#8217;ll be introduced to the concepts of recursion and higher-order functions, and understand why they&#8217;re often preferred over loops.</p>
<p>As you move on, you&#8217;ll delve into lists and pattern matching. You&#8217;ll learn how to create and add elements to lists in OCaml, and discover how they can be composed of different types using tuples. You&#8217;ll see the power of lists and tuples through practical examples of pattern matching.</p>
<p>Taking a step back, you’ll delve into higher-order functions, focusing on the functions that operate on lists such as List.map, List.filter, List.fold_left, and List.fold_right.</p>
<p>Finally, the course will cover advanced concepts like parametric polymorphism, which allows types with free variables to be replaced with any type, and inductive types, which are programmer-defined types created using the &#8220;type&#8221; keyword in OCaml. You&#8217;ll see an example of this by creating a &#8220;message&#8221; type with different constructors for string, bool, and float messages, and then defining a list of message types and writing a function that iterates over them.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course is 3–4 hours long. You’ll learn by watching the lecture videos, where you’ll see the instructor teaching the basics of the language as well as complete some practical exercises to recap what you’ve learned in the video.</p>

<h2 id="anchor-4">4. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/independent-ocaml-by-examples-121112" target="_blank" rel="noopener">OCaml By Example (O(1) Labs)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85427" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/4.-OCaml-By-Example-O1-Labs.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/4.-OCaml-By-Example-O1-Labs.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/4.-OCaml-By-Example-O1-Labs-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/4.-OCaml-By-Example-O1-Labs-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>Learn the OCaml language by following a series of examples in the <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/independent-ocaml-by-examples-121112" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Ocaml By Example course</a>!</p>
<p>No prior experience of OCaml is required to take this course.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>You’ll start this course with an overview of the basic language constructs such as values, functions, pattern matching, tuples, variants, lists, sets, arrays, and records. Although most of the concepts you’ll learn relate to functional programming, you’ll also understand how to program imperatively in OCaml as it is a multi-paradigm language.</p>
<p>Next, you’ll study data structures and algorithms, such as recursion, hash tables, and their implementation in the OCaml language. You’ll also understand the different ways to organize your code, such as modules and packages with the Dune build tool. Error handling and interacting with the file system are some other concepts you’ll also cover.</p>
<p>Finally, you’ll learn the more advanced parts of Ocaml, such as macros, and explore OCaml’s vast library collection, including interoperating with other programming languages such as C, JavaScript, and Rust.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course is made up of four chapters. You’ll learn by reading through the different articles along with the code examples provided.</p>

<h2 id="anchor-5">5. <a href="https://github.com/janestreet/learn-ocaml-workshop" target="_blank" rel="noopener">OCaml Workshop (Jane Street)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85428" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/5.-OCaml-Workshop-Jane-Street.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/5.-OCaml-Workshop-Jane-Street.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/5.-OCaml-Workshop-Jane-Street-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/5.-OCaml-Workshop-Jane-Street-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p><a href="https://github.com/janestreet/learn-ocaml-workshop" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Jane Street’s OCaml Workshop</a> aims to help people start developing in OCaml through small hands-on exercises and bigger, more complex projects like arcade games.</p>
<p>To take this workshop, you should have some experience with OCaml.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>After you get familiarized with OCaml’s build process and tools, you’ll complete twenty one exercises teaching you OCaml features such as pattern matching, higher order functions, options, and anonymous functions.</p>
<p>Once you get that covered, you’ll begin developing simplified clones of three arcade games: Snake, Lumines, and Frogger. Snake and Lumines both run on your computer, whereas Frogger runs on your web browser. Afterward, you can choose between several more advanced projects, such as writing a IRC bot, implementing <a href="https://github.com/junegunn/fzf" target="_blank" rel="noopener">command-line fuzzy finder</a>, or improving Frogger.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>Two types of exercises are given: small coding exercises and large projects. Small coding exercises test your understanding of different programming aspects of the OCaml language, whereas the larger projects provide the opportunity to apply your knowledge and skills to more complex, real-world problems. You’ll need to pass the `expect` tests in order to fully complete the exercises.</p>
<p>The course also provides a few paths you can take after completing the exercises, but these come without `expect` tests.</p>

<h2 id="anchor-6">6. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/independent-learn-ocaml-121114" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Learn OCaml (OCaml Software Foundation)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85429" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/6.-Learn-OCaml-OCaml-Software-Foundation.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/6.-Learn-OCaml-OCaml-Software-Foundation.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/6.-Learn-OCaml-OCaml-Software-Foundation-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/6.-Learn-OCaml-OCaml-Software-Foundation-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>OCaml Software Foundation’s <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/independent-learn-ocaml-121114" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Learn OCaml</a> site provides a variety of coding challenges for you to practice OCaml programming taken from Université de Paris OCaml courses.</p>
<p>Experience with OCaml is recommended to do the exercises.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>The difficulty of the exercises ranges from one star (very easy) to four stars (very hard).</p>
<p>Some of the easier exercises include searching for strings in arrays, balancing binary trees, and using first-class functions.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, the more difficult exercises include implementing algorithms such as merge sort and huffman compression, displaying a filesystem hierarchy, and developing a mini database.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>You’ll write and execute code directly in the browser’s coding environment. After each exercise, you’ll receive a grade based on how efficient your code is.</p>

<h2 id="anchor-7">7. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/exercism-ocaml-110604" target="_blank" rel="noopener">OCaml (Exercism)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85430" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/7.-OCaml-Exercism.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/7.-OCaml-Exercism.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/7.-OCaml-Exercism-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/7.-OCaml-Exercism-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/exercism-ocaml-110604" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Exercism</a> is an online coding platform that offers a variety of programming exercises and challenges that are suitable for all skill levels. It&#8217;s a great way to practice and improve your OCaml coding skills for <b>free</b>.</p>
<p>What makes Exercism stand out from other similar exercise providers is that it offers a <b>free </b>mentoring service. If you ever get stuck on an exercise or want to improve your code, you can request feedback from experienced OCaml programmers.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>Exercism offers exercises of varying difficulty levels, including easy, medium, and hard.</p>
<p>Examples of easy exercises include reporting leap years, calculating ages of people in a planet’s solar years, and determining if a sentence is a pangram.</p>
<p>Medium exercises include tasks such as counting the number of rectangles in an ASCII diagram, scoring a bowling game, and adding numbers to a minesweeper board.</p>
<p>For those looking for more of a challenge, there are also hard exercises available, such as calculating the date of meetups, implementing logic of hangman game using functional reactive programming, and creating a zipper for a binary tree.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course is self-paced, so you can take all the time you need to complete the 40+ hands-on programming exercises. Each exercise comes with automatic feedback of your code as well as personal mentoring to help you understand your code’s strengths and flaws.</p>

										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/coursera-free-courses.png"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-74380" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/coursera-free-courses.png" alt="Free courses on Coursera" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/coursera-free-courses.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/coursera-free-courses-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/coursera-free-courses-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Is Coursera Free?</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">At </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Class Central</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, we get that question so often that I wrote </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-signup-for-free/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">a guide to answer it</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Nowadays, most Coursera courses are free to audit. But if you want to complete graded assignments or get a course certificate, you have to pay.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera’s entire catalog used to be entirely free. But in late 2015, they </span><a href="https://blog.coursera.org/an-update-on-assessments-grades-and/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">introduced a paywall</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Over the following years, this monetization approach expanded to other online course providers, </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/edx-paywall-graded-assignments/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">including edX</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">But I always knew that there were a few courses on Coursera that remained completely free. When you enroll in these courses, they offer a “</span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Full Course, No Certificate</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">” option, as you can see below.</span></p>
<figure id="attachment_85413" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85413" style="width: 1536px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-course-no-certificate.png"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85413" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-course-no-certificate.png" alt="" width="1536" height="960" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-course-no-certificate.png 1536w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-course-no-certificate-300x188.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-course-no-certificate-1024x640.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-course-no-certificate-768x480.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1536px) 100vw, 1536px" /></a><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85413" class="wp-caption-text">Free Coursera course: “Full Course, No Certificate” option (with graded assignments)</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">By contrast, other courses tend to offer a more restrictive free-to-audit option, which doesn’t include graded assignments. This option is also quite easy to miss. You have to look for the “</span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">audit</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">” link at the very bottom of the window that pops up when you enroll.</span></p>
<figure id="attachment_85414" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85414" style="width: 1536px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-audit-course.png"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85414" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-audit-course.png" alt="" width="1536" height="1002" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-audit-course.png 1536w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-audit-course-300x196.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-audit-course-1024x668.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/coursera-free-audit-course-768x501.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1536px) 100vw, 1536px" /></a><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85414" class="wp-caption-text">Free Coursera course: Free audit option (without graded assignments)</figcaption></figure>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Which Courses are Entirely Free?</span></h2>
<div class="quote relative padding-horz-large xlarge-up-padding-horz-xxlarge padding-vert-xxsmall margin-bottom-large">
<p><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Out of Coursera’s 7000 or so active courses, I expected to find about 50 fully-free courses. Imagine my surprise (shock, really) when I found that close to 1700 Coursera courses are still completely free </span></em></p>
</div>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The biggest challenge is finding </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">which</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Coursera courses are entirely free. The Coursera website doesn’t provide any “free course” filter (</span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/provider/coursera?free=true"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Class Central does though</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> <img src="https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.1.0/72x72/1f60a.png" alt="😊" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" />). To know if a course is fully free, you have to log into Coursera, enroll in the course, and look for the “</span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Full Course, No Certificate</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">” option.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">But there are thousands of courses on Coursera, so short of checking them one by one, it’s tricky to manually put together a list of their fully-free courses. So instead, we went with an automated approach.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Originally, I used the browser automation tool </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subject/selenium"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Selenium</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> to check the courses for me. My colleague </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/@bob"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bob</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> set me up with an </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/institution/aws"><span style="font-weight: 400;">AWS instance</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and </span><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/cloud9/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Cloud9 IDE</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, where I could do this automation. Below is a screenshot of the setup. (Yes, I prefer PHP.)</span></p>
<figure id="attachment_85415" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85415" style="width: 1536px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/cloud9-selenium-php.png"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85415" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/cloud9-selenium-php.png" alt="" width="1536" height="950" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/cloud9-selenium-php.png 1536w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/cloud9-selenium-php-300x186.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/cloud9-selenium-php-1024x633.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/cloud9-selenium-php-768x475.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1536px) 100vw, 1536px" /></a><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85415" class="wp-caption-text">Automating the search for free Coursera courses with Selenium</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Out of Coursera’s 7000 or so active courses, I expected to find about 50 fully-free courses. Imagine my surprise (shock, really) when I found that close to 1700 Coursera courses are still completely free (that is, including the graded assignments, minus only the free certificate).</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Free Coursera Courses</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Below, I&#8217;ve compiled the 1700 entirely free courses offered on Coursera. </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">It includes a number of highly-rated courses, including a few from </span>Class Central’s <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/collection/top-free-online-courses">Best Online Courses of All Time</a>, such as Barbara Oakley&#8217;s <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/learning-how-to-learn-2161">Learning How to Learn</a>.</p>
<p>Here are some stats about the course list:</p>
<ul>
<li>Combined, these courses have <strong>76M</strong> enrollments.</li>
<li>Combined, they have received <strong>41K</strong> reviews on Class Central.</li>
<li>There are <strong>9</strong> courses with over <strong>1M</strong> enrollments.</li>
<li>The most popular one, <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/the-science-of-well-being-10346">Yale&#8217;s Science of Well-Being</a>, has <strong>4.3M </strong>enrollments.</li>
<li><strong>58%</strong> of the courses are in English and <strong>14%</strong> are in Spanish.</li>
</ul>
